  Windsurf ChatGPT said: Thought for 21s Alright Alin â€” hereâ€™s the clean, final
  setup that stops the thrash: correct InstaWP MCP-WP config, tight
  orchestrator handoffs, strict agent boundaries, duplicate-safe publishing,
  and image/product validation. Copy-paste the blocks as-is. 0) TL;DR order of
  operations Configure and run the InstaWP WordPress MCP server Point your MCP
  client (Windsurf/Claude Desktop) at it Patch your agents with the drop-in
  sections below (writer scope, slug lookup, image headers, whitelist) Run the
  sanity checks to prove everything works end-to-end Use the one-command
  pipeline for the TVA article 1) InstaWP MCP-WP: minimal, correct config 1.1
  Create a dedicated WP Application Password (Editor or Author is enough)
  WordPress â†’ Users â†’ Profile â†’ Application Passwords Name it mcp-wp-editor,
  copy the generated pass (keep the spaces, they matter to WP, MCP will strip
  them). 1.2 Create the server .env Put this next to where youâ€™ll run the
  server (e.g. ~/mcp-wp/.env) # WordPress site WP_URL=https://inteles.ro
  WP_USER=alin@example.com WP_APP_PASSWORD=xxxx xxxx xxxx xxxx # Optional hard
  timeouts (seconds) HTTP_TIMEOUT=30 MCP_STDIO=false LOG_LEVEL=info 1.3 Run the
  server (npx) npx -y @instawp/mcp-wp You should see: MCP WordPress server
  listening ... tools registered: list_posts, get_post, create_post,
  update_post, create_media ... Optional: Docker (if you prefer) docker run
  --rm -it --name mcp-wp \ -e WP_URL="https://inteles.ro" \ -e
  WP_USER="alin@example.com" \ -e WP_APP_PASSWORD="xxxx xxxx xxxx xxxx" \
  ghcr.io/instawp/mcp-wp:latest 2) Point your client at the server (Windsurf
  MCP config) Add this block to your Windsurf mcpServers: { "mcpServers":
  { "instawp-wp": { "serverUrl": "http://localhost:3355/mcp", "headers": { "X-
  MCP-Client": "Windsurf" }, "disabled": false } } } If your server prints a
  different URL/port, use that. If you expose it remotely, keep it behind
  HTTPS. 3) Drop-in fixes for your agents (surgical; wonâ€™t break your path-only
  design) 3.1 Orchestrator (CLAUDE.md): robust post lookup + duplicate-safe
  publish Paste this exact block into CLAUDE.md under â€œWordPress fetch &
  duplicate detectionâ€: ## WORDPRESS FETCH & DUPLICATE DETECTION (REQUIRED) #
  Input: a WordPress URL or title. # Goal: load the article text for editing;
  later publish as UPDATE if it exists, CREATE if not. ### When given a URL: 1)
  Extract slug strictly: - Lowercase, keep hyphens: e.g. https://inteles.ro/
  tva-in-romania-ghid-complet-2025-2/ â†’ "tva-in-romania-ghid-complet-2025-2" 2)
  Find the post using minimal result windows (prevent token bloat): - Try:
  list_posts(search="<slug>", per_page=1, status="publish", page=1) - If none:
  repeat with status="draft" then "pending" then "private" (per_page=1 each) -
  If still none: fall back to exact title search with per_page=1 3) If found: -
  get_post(id) - Extract clean plaintext for editing - Set: operation="update",
  post_id=<id> 4) If not found: - Fetch page HTML via WebFetch (only as last
  resort), clean to plaintext - Set: operation="create" ### Before publish: -
  Compute slug from the new articleâ€™s title (kebab-case; preserve diacritics in
  body, not slug) - Re-run list_posts(search="<slug>", per_page=1,
  status="publish") to guard against duplicates introduced during editing. - If
  found: operation="update", post_id=<id>; else: operation="create". 3.2 Writer
  controller (content-quickfire.md): hard scope guardrails Append this
  â€œCRITICAL SCOPEâ€ block: ## CRITICAL SCOPE (DO NOT REMOVE) - Your ONLY job:
  produce the article markdown and save it to disk. - Do NOT search or download
  images. - Do NOT look for affiliate products or links. - Do NOT call
  WordPress or publish. - Output only: an absolute file path to the saved .md.
  Return exactly one line containing ONLY the absolute file path. 3.3 Image
  Curator (inteles-image-curator.md): deterministic output + path checks
  Append: ## INPUT - file_path: absolute path to the markdown file ## STEPS 1)
  Read the file at file_path; strip markdown to plaintext for analysis. 2) Plan
  4â€“6 images max (hero + inline). Keep 1 asset per major section. 3) Acquire
  images (via Pexels MCP or local set), convert to WebP, write EXIF-free. 4)
  File existence gate: verify each path exists (`test -f` equivalent). 5)
  Produce structured JSON ONLY. ## OUTPUT (JSON, no prose) { "images":
  [ { "role": "hero|inline|gallery", "file": "tva-2025-hero.webp", "path": "/
  home/alin/DATA/OBSIDIAN/inteles-vault/10-Assets/pexels/processed/tva-2025-
  hero.webp", "alt": "ExplicaÈ›ie clarÄƒ a TVA-ului Ã®n RomÃ¢nia Ã®n 2025, calcul la
  birou", "caption": null, "priority": 1, "insertion_point":
  "after_paragraph_2" } ], "notes": "one sentence max" } ## QUALITY GATES -
  WebP only; absolute paths; Romanian ALT 50â€“125 chars; 1 image/section; hero
  present. - If any check fails, regenerate that item and re-validate before
  returning. 3.4 Monetizer (romanian-affiliate-product-finder.md): whitelist
  only Append: ## AFFILIATE WHITELIST (REQUIRED) - Read: /home/alin/DATA/
  OBSIDIAN/inteles-vault/04-Monetization/affiliates.csv - Extract approved
  merchant domains. - Return ONLY product URLs from approved domains. - Reject
  Amazon/eBay/generic searches/homepages. ## OUTPUT (one URL per line, no extra
  text) https://partner.ro/produs-1 https://partner.ro/produs-2 https://
  partner.ro/produs-3 ## IF NONE FOUND Return an empty output (no
  placeholders). 3.5 WordPress Publisher (wordpress-publisher.md): headers,
  chunking, placement Append: ## INPUT CONTRACT { "operation": "create|update",
  "post_id": "<id when update>", "article_path": "/abs/path/to/article.md",
  "images": [...], // from Image Curator JSON "products": [ {"url":
  "..."}, ... ] // from Monetizer (validated) } ## MEDIA UPLOAD (FIX) For each
  image: - create_media( source_url: "file://<absolute_path>", title:
  "<slug>-<role>-<priority>", alt_text: "<romanian-alt>", caption:
  "<optional>" ) - Server will set: Content-Type: image/webp Content-
  Disposition: attachment; filename="<file>" - Capture media id + source_url
  and map into HTML. ## CHUNKED CONTENT (AVOID TOKEN OVERFLOW) - Read markdown,
  convert to HTML. - Split into â‰¤ 5k-token chunks on paragraph/heading
  boundaries. - Insert images at declared "insertion_point" between chunks. -
  Insert product blocks sparsely (max 4 total, never adjacent to an image in
  the same paragraph). ## CREATE vs UPDATE - If operation="update": call
  update_post(id, ...) and preserve existing featured image unless a new hero
  is provided. - If operation="create": create_post(...) ## HARD VALIDATIONS -
  Verify every image path exists before upload. - Products count 0â€“4; each URL
  matches whitelist (publisher double-check). - Abort if post content hash
  unchanged on update (prevent duplicate no-op publish). 4) Sanity tests (prove
  the pipeline before you hit â€œrealâ€) 4.1 Quick tool ping (from the MCP client)
  Use your MCP clientâ€™s â€œList toolsâ€ â†’ ensure you see list_posts, get_post,
  create_post, update_post, create_media. 4.2 Slug search (exact, low result
  window) list_posts(search="tva-in-romania-ghid-complet-2025-2", per_page=1,
  status="publish", page=1) If [], repeat with status="draft", then pending,
  then private. 4.3 Media upload dry-run (local file) Pick any small webp you
  own: create_media( source_url="file:///home/alin/DATA/OBSIDIAN/inteles-
  vault/10-Assets/pexels/processed/test.webp", title="sanity-test",
  alt_text="Imagine test ALT Ã®n limba romÃ¢nÄƒ", caption="" ) Expect a media.id
  and a WordPress URL back. If not: check app password / file path / server
  logs. 5) One-command pipeline for the TVA article Use this exact invocation
  flow inside your agent runner (no edits needed if you added the blocks
  above): Fetch/decide create vs update (orchestrator auto-handles via slug
  loop) content-quickfire â†’ returns ONLY the markdown path in parallel:
  inteles-image-curator with file_path romanian-affiliate-product-finder with
  file_path wordpress-publisher receives: operation + optional post_id

0) TL;DR order of operations
   Configure and run the InstaWP WordPress MCP server
   
   Point your MCP client (Windsurf/Claude Desktop) at it
   
   Patch your agents with the drop-in sections below (writer scope, slug lookup,
   image headers, whitelist)
   
   Run the sanity checks to prove everything works end-to-end
   
   Use the one-command pipeline for the TVA article

1) InstaWP MCP-WP: minimal, correct config
   1.1 Create a dedicated WP Application Password (Editor or Author is enough)
   WordPress â†’ Users â†’ Profile â†’ Application Passwords
   Name it mcp-wp-editor, copy the generated pass (keep the spaces, they matter
   to WP, MCP will strip them).
   
   1.2 Create the server .env
   Put this next to where youâ€™ll run the server (e.g. ~/mcp-wp/.env)
   
   # WordPress site
   
   WP_URL=https://inteles.ro
   WP_USER=alin@example.com
   WP_APP_PASSWORD=xxxx xxxx xxxx xxxx
   
   # Optional hard timeouts (seconds)
   
   HTTP_TIMEOUT=30
   MCP_STDIO=false
   LOG_LEVEL=info
   1.3 Run the server (npx)
   npx -y @instawp/mcp-wp
   You should see: MCP WordPress server listening ... tools registered:
   list_posts, get_post, create_post, update_post, create_media ...
   
   Optional: Docker (if you prefer)
   docker run --rm -it --name mcp-wp \
   -e WP_URL="https://inteles.ro" \
   -e WP_USER="alin@example.com" \
   -e WP_APP_PASSWORD="xxxx xxxx xxxx xxxx" \
   ghcr.io/instawp/mcp-wp:latest

2) Point your client at the server (Windsurf MCP config)
   Add this block to your Windsurf mcpServers:
   
   {
   "mcpServers": {
    "instawp-wp": {
      "serverUrl": "http://localhost:3355/mcp",
      "headers": {
   
        "X-MCP-Client": "Windsurf"
   
      },
      "disabled": false
    }
   }
   }
   If your server prints a different URL/port, use that. If you expose it
   remotely, keep it behind HTTPS.

3) Drop-in fixes for your agents (surgical; wonâ€™t break your path-only
   design)
   3.1 Orchestrator (CLAUDE.md): robust post lookup + duplicate-safe publish
   Paste this exact block into CLAUDE.md under â€œWordPress fetch & duplicate
   detectionâ€:
   
   ## WORDPRESS FETCH & DUPLICATE DETECTION (REQUIRED)
   
   # Input: a WordPress URL or title.
   
   # Goal: load the article text for editing; later publish as UPDATE if it
   
   exists, CREATE if not.
   
   ### When given a URL:

4) Extract slug strictly:
   
   - Lowercase, keep hyphens: e.g. https://inteles.ro/tva-in-romania-ghid-
     complet-2025-2/ â†’ "tva-in-romania-ghid-complet-2025-2"

5) Find the post using minimal result windows (prevent token bloat):
   
   - Try: list_posts(search="<slug>", per_page=1, status="publish", page=1)
   - If none: repeat with status="draft" then "pending" then
     "private" (per_page=1 each)
   - If still none: fall back to exact title search with per_page=1

6) If found:
   
   - get_post(id)
   - Extract clean plaintext for editing
   - Set: operation="update", post_id=<id>

7) If not found:
   
   - Fetch page HTML via WebFetch (only as last resort), clean to plaintext
   - Set: operation="create"
   
   ### Before publish:
- Compute slug from the new articleâ€™s title (kebab-case; preserve diacritics
  in body, not slug)

- Re-run list_posts(search="<slug>", per_page=1, status="publish") to guard
  against duplicates introduced during editing.

- All URLs MUST be from known affiliate partners
- Reject Amazon, eBay, generic product pages
- Empty product list is acceptable (proceed without)
- Max 4 products total

### Duplicate Prevention

- Always check slug before publishing
- If slug exists â†’ operation="update"
- If slug missing â†’ operation="create"
- Never allow two posts with same slug

---

## ERROR HANDLING

| Error | Cause | Action |
|-------|-------|--------|
| `Tool not found: get_post` | Deprecated tool | Use `get_content_by_slug`
instead |
| `status: "any" invalid` | Wrong enum | Use specific status: "publish",
"draft", etc. |
| `MCP response too large` | Broad search | Use `per_page: 1` and exact slug
|
| Image curator fails | Download/processing error | Retry once; if fails,
proceed without images |
| Monetizer returns non-partners | Partner validation missing | Reject and
ask to retry with partner URLs only |
| Duplicate slug detected | Pre-publish check failed | Stop and ask user:
update or create new? |

---

## SUCCESS CHECKLIST

- [ ] Phase 1: Article fetched/cleaned
- [ ] Phase 2: FILE_PATH captured from content-quickfire
- [ ] Phase 3a: Images returned with paths + insertion points
- [ ] Phase 3b: Products returned from partners only
- [ ] Phase 4: Duplicate check completed (slug search done)
- [ ] Phase 5: wordpress-publisher called with operation + post_id
- [ ] Final: Post URL returned to user

---

## Quick Reference: inteles-wordpress MCP Tools

find_content_by_url(url) â†’ Full content object
get_content_by_slug(slug, content_type) â†’ Single post/page
list_content(content_type, search, per_page, status) â†’ List (always per_page:
1)
create_content(content_type, title, content, status, excerpt, featured_media,
categories) â†’ New post
update_content(id, content_type, title, content, ...) â†’ Update existing
create_media(source_url, title, alt_text, caption) â†’ Upload image

text

**Remember:** Every tool requires `content_type: "post"` or `"page"`. Never
omit it.

# WordPress Publisher for inteles.ro (Production-Ready)

## CORE MISSION

Transform article + images + products into live WordPress posts via
**inteles-wordpress MCP only**. Idempotent, duplicate-safe, Kadence-ready.

---

## INPUT CONTRACT (STRICT JSON)

{
"article_path": "/absolute/path/article.md",
"operation": "create|update",
"post_id": 123,
"images": [
{
"filename": "hero.webp",
"path": "/absolute/path/hero.webp",
"role": "hero|inline|gallery",
"alt": "Romanian description",
"caption": null,
"insertion_point": "after_intro",
"priority": 1
}
],
"products": [
"https://partner.ro/product-1",
"https://partner.ro/product-2"
]
}

text

---

## PHASE 1: VALIDATION

1. **Verify operation is valid:**
   - `operation` = "create" or "update" only
   - If "update": `post_id` must be present and numeric

2. **Verify article file exists:**
   - `article_path` must be absolute path
   - File must exist and be readable
   - Extract title and content from file

3. **Verify images:**
   - All files MUST exist on disk (check before touching WordPress)
   - All MUST be WebP format (extension: .webp)
   - All alt text MUST be Romanian, â‰¥5 words
   - At least one hero image MUST be present
   - If any image missing: ABORT with file path in error

4. **Verify products:**
   - Each URL must be valid HTTPS
   - No Amazon, eBay, or generic product pages
   - If list empty: OK (proceed without products)

**If validation fails, return immediately:**
{
"success": false,
"stage": "validation",
"error": "Detailed reason",
"failed_item": "/path/to/missing/file"
}

text

---

## PHASE 2: MEDIA UPLOAD & REUSE

For each image (priority order):

### Step 1: Check if file exists

test -f /absolute/path/file.webp && echo "exists" || echo "missing"

text

If missing: **ABORT immediately** with file path

### Step 2: Try to reuse existing media

Call inteles-wordpress MCP:
inteles-wordpress - list_media(
search: "filename-without-extension",
per_page: 3
)

text

**If exact filename match found:** Reuse that media ID and URL (skip upload)

**If not found:** Proceed to upload

### Step 3: Upload new media

Call inteles-wordpress MCP:
inteles-wordpress - create_media(
source_url: "file:///absolute/path/hero.webp",
title: "slug-role-priority",
alt_text: "Romanian descriptive text",
caption: "Optional Romanian caption or null"
)

text

**Returns:**
{
"id": 456,
"source_url": "https://inteles.ro/wp-content/uploads/..."
}

text

**CRITICAL:** inteles-wordpress MCP handles all headers automatically
(Content-Type, Content-Disposition).

### Step 4: Track media mapping

Store: `{role: {id, url, file}}`

Designate hero image ID as `featured_media_id`

---

## PHASE 3: HTML CONSTRUCTION

1. **Read article file** from `article_path`
2. **Convert markdown to HTML** (preserve any Kadence block comments)
3. **Patch image placeholders:**
   - Find: `[hero.url]`, `IMAGE_HERO`, `{{hero}}`, etc.
   - Replace with: actual media URL from Phase 2
   - Find: `wp-image-PLACEHOLDER`, `image-id-hero`, etc.
   - Replace with: actual media ID, e.g., `wp-image-456`

4. **Preserve Kadence blocks:**
   - Keep all `<!-- wp:kadence/... -->` comments intact
   - Do not modify block attributes or data
   - Keep JSON configurations untouched

5. **Insert product links** (if provided):
   - Max 4 products total
   - Create Kadence custom HTML blocks:
<!-- wp:kadence/advancedhtml --> <div class="kb-html"> <div class="product-
recommendation"> <a href="https://partner.ro/product-1" rel="nofollow
sponsored noopener" target="_blank"> <strong>Product Title</strong> - Brief
description </a> </div> </div> <!-- /wp:kadence/advancedhtml --> ``` - Always
include: `rel="nofollow sponsored noopener"` - Place naturally (after
paragraphs, not clustered)
Sanitize content:

Remove any <script> or <style> tags (not part of Kadence)

Strip inline styles that conflict with theme

Preserve Romanian diacritics perfectly (Äƒ, Ã¢, Ã®, È™, È›)

PHASE 4: POST DISCOVERY (for updates)
If operation: "update" and post_id provided:

Use that post_id directly â†’ skip to Phase 5b

If operation: "create":

Proceed to Phase 5a (create)

PHASE 5A: CREATE NEW POST
Call inteles-wordpress MCP:

text
inteles-wordpress - create_content(
  content_type: "post",
  title: "Article Title",
  content: "<patched HTML from Phase 3>",
  status: "publish",
  excerpt: "25â€“45 word Romanian summary",
  featured_media: 456,
  categories:
)
CRITICAL PARAMETERS:

content_type = "post" (always)

status = "publish" (not "any")

featured_media = hero image ID from Phase 2

categories = â€‹ (ÃnÈ›elesul Viselor)

Returns:

text
{
  "id": 789,
  "link": "https://inteles.ro/article-slug/",
  "status": "publish"
}
PHASE 5B: UPDATE EXISTING POST
Call inteles-wordpress MCP:

text
inteles-wordpress - update_content(
  id: 123,
  content_type: "post",
  title: "Article Title",
  content: "<patched HTML from Phase 3>",
  status: "publish",
  excerpt: "25â€“45 word Romanian summary",
  featured_media: 456,
  categories:
)
CRITICAL: Always preserve existing featured image unless new hero provided

Returns: Updated post object with ID and link

PHASE 6: VERIFICATION
Verify response contains valid post ID

Confirm status = "publish"

Validate post URL contains correct slug

Confirm featured_media set correctly

Check all media uploads succeeded

}
CRITICAL MCP TOOL RULES
âœ… ALWAYS DO:
Use get_content_by_slug BEFORE creating (duplicate check)

Use create_content / update_content with content_type: "post"

Use create_media with source_url: "file://..." for local files

Set featured_media to hero image ID

Set status: "publish" and categories: [5]

Verify files exist before uploading

âŒ NEVER DO:
Use deprecated tools: create_post, update_post, get_post, list_posts

Use status: "any" (invalid)

Upload media without verifying file exists

Forget content_type parameter

Use relative file paths

Create duplicate posts without checking slug first

AUTO-FIX FALLBACKS
Issue    Fix
Tool not found: create_post    Use create_content with content_type: "post"
status: "any" invalid    Use specific: "publish", "draft", "pending"
Media upload fails    Check file exists, verify .webp format, retry once
Duplicate slug detected    Stop, ask user: update or create new?
Missing featured_media    Abort, user must provide at least one hero image
Product URL non-partner    Remove from list, proceed with valid products only
EDGE CASES
What if article has no products?
â†’ OK, proceed without product links. Products array can be empty.

What if all images fail to upload?
â†’ Log error, proceed without images, note in response.

What if article file is corrupted/unreadable?
â†’ Abort with clear file path error.

What if article title is very long?
â†’ Truncate intelligently at word boundary, keep title â‰¤120 chars.

What if excerpt exceeds 45 words?
â†’ Truncate at sentence boundary, warn in response.

    - Optional partner-domain double-check for product links.
    - Auto-fixes for status:"any", missing per_page, and broad searches.

Key File Spots

- CLAUDE.md:143 adds â€œWORDPRESS FETCH & DUPLICATE DETECTION (REQUIRED)â€
- CLAUDE.md:162 adds â€œTOKEN EFFICIENCY RULES (MUST FOLLOW)â€

Why This Fixes Your Errors

- Prevents token overflow: all list_content calls are per_page: 1 and slug-
  only.
- Blocks deprecated tools: no get_post, list_posts, create_post, update_post.
- No status:"any": strict status retry matrix.
- Duplicate-safe: re-checks slug pre-publish to decide update vs create.
- Media robust: existence checks, reuse-before-upload, file:// source for
  local files.

Quick Sanity Tests

- Post lookup (publish then drafts):
    - list_content("post", search="<exact-slug>", per_page=1,
      status="publish")

â”€ Worked for 1m 28s â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â€¢ Short answer: the orchestrator is hitting the MCP with the wrong tools and
parameters because your server only exposes legacy endpoints, and the general
agent then â€œhelpfullyâ€ broadens the search, causing token blowups and misses.

Whatâ€™s actually happening

- Tool mismatch: Your inteles-wordpress MCP appears to expose legacy tools
  (list_posts, get_post, etc.), not find_content_by_url/get_content_by_slug/
  list_content. The general agent fell back to legacy tools.
- Bad parameters: It used after, orderby:"slug", and a broad search term
  (â€œtvaâ€) with per_page: 5, which triggered the 72k+ token overflow and empty
  matches.
- Wrong delegation: Previously it tried to make the writer call MCP; we
  blocked that. The orchestrator must call MCP itself.

What I changed (CLAUDE.md)

- Hard block: Orchestrator calls inteles-wordpress itself (never delegates MCP
  to writer).
- Primary path: find_content_by_url â†’ get_content_by_slug â†’ list_content with
  per_page:1 and exact slug.
- Legacy fallback (only if preferred tools are missing): strict allowlist
  for list_posts:
    - search: exact slug only (no spaces, no partials)
    - per_page: 1, page: 1
    - status sequence: publish â†’ draft â†’ pending â†’ private
    - forbidden: after, orderby, order, any broad search (e.g., â€œTVAâ€),
      per_page > 1
    - optionally get_post(id) only if you truly need the full object
- Exception note: explicitly says when and only how to use legacy tools; keeps
  token usage tiny.

Publisher agent

- Already strict and fine. It permits legacy fallbacks safely inside the
  publisher only for slug discovery; not related to your current failure
  point.

How to test the fix (single exact calls)

- Lookup (legacy-safe if new tools missing):
    - inteles-wordpress - list_posts(search:"tva-in-romania-ghid-complet-2025-
      2", per_page:1, page:1, status:"publish")
    - If [], retry same call with status:"draft", then "pending", then
      "private"
    - Do not add after/orderby/order; do not broaden search; do not change
      per_page
- If still [], WebFetch is allowed as last resort to get plaintext for writer
  (as your run did).

Root-cause summary

- The general agent broadened parameters (after/orderby/broad search/
  per_page>1) on legacy endpoints. Thatâ€™s why it overflowed and missed the
  post. The updated CLAUDE.md now hard-limits the legacy shape to exact-slug +
  per_page:1 only and bans broadening, so the agent stops thrashing and stays
  token-efficient.

If you want, I can also pin an explicit â€œparameter allowlistâ€ block at the
top of CLAUDE.md to make it even harder for the agent to drift, but the Legacy
section I added should be enough.

â€¢ Hereâ€™s what I found and fixed in the wordpress-publisher agent to stop the
drift and make it publish-only, token-efficient, and aligned with your live
MCP server.

Snags Identified

- Over-broad tool access encouraged drift:
    - Allowed â€œSkillâ€, WebFetch/WebSearch, Perplexity, and many WP tools
      unrelated to publishing, which led to subagent calls and off-path
      behavior. See .claude/agents/wordpress-publisher.md:4.
- Missing modern lookup tools in header:
    - File referenced find_content_by_url, get_content_by_slug, list_content
      in prose, but they were not whitelisted in the tools: header. This
      pushed the agent toward list_posts/get_post, causing token bloat and
      bad queries.
- Contradictory guidance on endpoints:
    - Bottom â€œQuick Referenceâ€ told the agent to use non-existent
      create_content/update_content and refused create_post/update_post, while
      your server actually exposes and uses create_post/update_post.
- Subagent delegation from Publisher:
    - Nothing prevented the agent from calling other agents (writer, image-
      curator, monetizer), causing â€œUnknown skill: â€¦â€ errors and wasted
      tokens.
- No â€œpublish-as-isâ€ mode:
    - When you hand over a ready HTML file, the publisher still tried to read/
      write other files and patch images or call subagents.

Fixes Applied (surgical)

- Tight tool allowlist (MCP only; no Skill or web tools)
    - Replaced the huge tool list with only whatâ€™s needed for publishing and
      media:
        - Lookup: find_content_by_url, get_content_by_slug, list_content
        - Publish: create_post, update_post
        - Media: list_media, create_media, get_media, edit_media
    - File: .claude/agents/wordpress-publisher.md:4
- Enforced PUBLISH-ONLY mode
    - Added a hard block to forbid calling other agents and to publish given
      HTML exactly as-is when provided. File: .claude/agents/wordpress-
      publisher.md:24
- Added â€œPublish-As-Isâ€ trigger
    - Input contract now supports article_path and publish_as_is: true to
      short-circuit any enrichment and publish the HTML content directly.
      File: .claude/agents/wordpress-publisher.md:100
    - Execution protocol short-circuits Phase 3/4 when publish_as_is is used.
      File: .claude/agents/wordpress-publisher.md:112
- Canonicalized publish endpoints to match your server
    - Publication now prefers create_post / update_post (with slug) and
      removed all â€œcreate_content/update_contentâ€ usage (except where noted
      the server also has page endpoints). File: .claude/agents/wordpress-
      publisher.md:230
- Corrected Quick Reference
    - â€œALWAYS DOâ€ now reflects create_post/update_post, explicit per_page:1
      for lookups, create_media source_url handling, and â€œNEVER DOâ€ blocks
      broad searches/status:any/subagent calls. File: .claude/agents/
      wordpress-publisher.md:357
    - Example flow shows proper publish via create_post, not create_content.
      File: .claude/agents/wordpress-publisher.md:379

Why this fixes your observed issues

- Unknown skill errors (â€œcontent-quickfireâ€, â€œinteles-image-curatorâ€):
  Removing Skill and adding a strict â€œNO SUBAGENTSâ€ section prevents this.
- Token overflow on list_posts: Header now exposes the modern lookup tools and
  instruction forbids list_posts; lookups require exact slug and per_page:1.
- â€œNicio dispoziÈ›ie de conÈ›inut furnizatÄƒâ€: The doc emphasizes create_media
  must include a valid source_url (file:// or https://) and validates paths
  before use.
- â€œJust push the article as isâ€: The publish_as_is toggle and article_path
  support now enforce direct publication of your HTML without creating other
  files, research, or image/product work.

- Tools allowlist minimized and corrected: .claude/agents/wordpress-
  publisher.md:4
